  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_9c1d957a-da96-456d-b219-9ecf4e3dcdff'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();

      initializeSiwa();

<span id="freeTextContainer12749974421542592885">Another fun time reading a classic and nostalgia filled book to my kids!<br/><br/>Probably the best part of the experience was when it came to sharing my progress on Goodreads and the wide array of responses I got. Everything from, “Wow, I haven’t read this in years! I was one of my favorites!” to, “WHAT THE HECK ARE YOU READING!” I mean, it is a book about a vampire bunny and if you saw the cover come across your feed, and you had never heard of it, you might have had a similar shocked reaction!<br/><br/>I did enj</span>
  <span id="freeText12749974421542592885" style="display:none">Another fun time reading a classic and nostalgia filled book to my kids!<br /><br />Probably the best part of the experience was when it came to sharing my progress on Goodreads and the wide array of responses I got. Everything from, “Wow, I haven’t read this in years! I was one of my favorites!” to, “WHAT THE HECK ARE YOU READING!” I mean, it is a book about a vampire bunny and if you saw the cover come across your feed, and you had never heard of it, you might have had a similar shocked reaction!<br /><br />I did enjoy reading this to my kids and have enjoyed the fact that they have now consumed three straight books one chapter a night with great enthusiasm. However, unlike Charlie and the Chocolate factory, it did not quite translate to a 5-star read for me as an adult and, if I had not been enjoying it along with my kids I might have not enjoyed it quite as much. But, still, a classic!<br /><br />One of my favorite things about this book is that it does have a similar feel to Dracula in the narration by Harold the dog. His delivery and diction felt very similar to Harker’s letters in Dracula. That was a really cool connection – and I hope if my kids get to read Dracula some day they remember Bunnicula!<br /><br />So, either enjoy a nostalgic “horror” trip to your childhood or continue to be confused as to why someone would want to read this. Either way, Bunnicula is not going anywhere in the annals of classic youth literature<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12749974421542592885" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_976477287" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/976477287" />
    <a title="Brandon Sanderson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3145554-brandon-sanderson"><img alt="Brandon Sanderson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1394044413p2/3145554.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/976477287?book_show_action=true">Jun 24, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brandon Sanderson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brandon Sanderson" href="/user/show/3145554-brandon-sanderson">Brandon Sanderson</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer976477287" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12194995298459295743">(This review is from 2004.)<br/><br/>Since it’s Halloween, I thought I’d talk about something frightening: Bunnies. Vampire bunnies. Ninja vampire bunnies. Okay, so, maybe not that ninja part. But definitely vampire bunnies—one in particular.<br/><br/>So, my roommate (Mr. “I’m not in there!” from the other week) was recently given a collection of young adult books as a birthday present. Most of the stack didn’t interest me, but I did notice one specific volume in the pile. I remember reading <i>Bunnicula</i> as a child, a</span>
  <span id="freeText12194995298459295743" style="display:none">(This review is from 2004.)<br /><br />Since it’s Halloween, I thought I’d talk about something frightening: Bunnies. Vampire bunnies. Ninja vampire bunnies. Okay, so, maybe not that ninja part. But definitely vampire bunnies—one in particular.<br /><br />So, my roommate (Mr. “I’m not in there!” from the other week) was recently given a collection of young adult books as a birthday present. Most of the stack didn’t interest me, but I did notice one specific volume in the pile. I remember reading <i>Bunnicula</i> as a child, and it very well could have been my first genre fiction book ever. So, intrigued about how I would regard the experience as an adult, I sat down one evening to give the novel another read.<br /><br />I came out of it with two impressions. First, that is one amazingly fun book. Second, that is one amazingly short book.<br /><br />On the second point, it turns out that I’m older now—and I’m used to stories that take a little bit longer to tell. It’s pretty amazing how few words they managed to pack into so many pages. (It’s around a hundred, give or take, depending on your edition.) It’s short. It has chapters, true, but they’re. . .well, more like extended paragraphs. I was through the book before I knew what had happened.<br /><br />Part of that, however, was due to sheer enjoyment. Often times, when I look back at things I enjoyed as a child, I find that I displayed an embarrassing lack of discerning taste. (<i>G.I. Joe</i>—or pretty much any cartoon I watched—makes a fine example.) <i>Bunnicula</i>, however, was a delightful read—both because of how fun it was, and because it proves that I at least had good taste in books when I was young. (Even if my TV habits were deplorable.)<br /><br />Anyway, about the book itself. Aspiring writers, take note—there are a wealth of lessons to be learned from this humble story. First off, it has an interesting premise. A normal family discovers a mysterious pet bunny abandoned in a movie theater—a bunny that turns out to have belonged to Dracula, and how goes out during the night to hunt vegetables and drain their ‘blood.’ Amusing, perhaps a bit farcical—however, the authors manage to mix this potentially-ridiculous idea with some solid storytelling. The book is told from the viewpoint of the family’s pet dog, a creature with a healthy dose of personality and an interesting narrative style.<br /><br />That means we have both a clever premise, a strong character, and a unique viewpoint. Mix with that a solid mystery plot—why are these white vegetables appearing around the house, and why does that bunny look so downright evil?—and you have a book that will hold its own against pretty much anything you throw at it. I know a lot of modern fantasy novels that could learn a few things from <i>Bunnicula</i>.<br /><br />So, I recommend that you give the book a read, if you haven’t already. It’s fun, quick, and could probably teach you a few things. And, if you did read the book as a child, it might be an interesting experience to pick it up—like I did—and see how your childhood memories compare to your adult observations.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12194995298459295743" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_127121967" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/127121967" />
    <a title="Alex" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3144945-alex"><img alt="Alex" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594856152p2/3144945.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/127121967?book_show_action=true">Oct 20, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alex" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alex" href="/user/show/3144945-alex">Alex</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3144945-alex?shelf=good-dogs">good-dogs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3144945-alex?shelf=children">children</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3144945-alex?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3144945-alex?shelf=gothic">gothic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer127121967" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11783077271764995539">Hear me out: there is no Bunnicula. This is about the cat.<br/><br/>His name is Chester. He has schemes and a vivid imagination, as cats do. He's steeped in <a href='https://www.theguardian.com/books/interactive/2014/may/09/reading-gothic-novel-pictures' rel='nofollow noopener'>Gothic literature.</a> Here's <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1218225518' rel='nofollow noopener'>my Gothic Drinking Game</a> if you need a refresher, and notice how Bunnicula will get you drunk:<blockquote>
<br/>- Nasty weather<br/>- Fainting (in our first hint that Bunnicula may not be the villain, he is usually the fainter)<br/>- Creepy noises<br/>- Scary eyes<br/>- And the most important thing: a relative turns out to be the surprise villain. </blockquote><br/>Here's what we </span>
  <span id="freeText11783077271764995539" style="display:none">Hear me out: there is no Bunnicula. This is about the cat.<br><br>His name is Chester. He has schemes and a vivid imagination, as cats do. He's steeped in <a href="https://www.theguardian.com/books/interactive/2014/may/09/reading-gothic-novel-pictures" rel="nofollow noopener">Gothic literature.</a> Here's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1218225518" rel="nofollow noopener">my Gothic Drinking Game</a> if you need a refresher, and notice how Bunnicula will get you drunk:<blockquote>
<br>- Nasty weather<br>- Fainting (in our first hint that Bunnicula may not be the villain, he is usually the fainter)<br>- Creepy noises<br>- Scary eyes<br>- And the most important thing: a relative turns out to be the surprise villain. </blockquote><br>Here's what we know: the Monroes have a new bunny, and vegetables are turning white. The bunny has funny markings, which leads the family to name him Bunnicula. On this evidence Chester declares the bunny a vampire. This is basically the plot of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1068108443" title="My review of Jane Austen's Gothic homage" rel="nofollow noopener">Northanger Abbey.</a><br><br>This would be funny if Chester's reaction wasn't so unbelievably cruel: he immediately starts stealing all the food from the bunny's cage, to keep the bunny from murdering lettuce. Bunnicula is young. Chester is starving a baby bunny to death because he says it's a vampire. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1518443977i/25046515._SY540_.jpg" alt="bunnicula" width="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>One of the original illustrations, which are great, basically lays out the whole plot</i><br><br>The book is narrated by the family dog, who plays himself off as stupid but also insists he recognizes and understands Romanian, so it's safe to call him unreliable. Anyway dogs are the least reliable of narrators, have you ever tried to let one explain what they're smelling?<br><br>The poor family finally realizes Bunnicula is on the brink of death and rushes him to the vet, who prescribes carrot juice, so the poor thing is saved in the nick of time. The rabbit has still never said a word; there's been no evidence whatsoever that he's a vampire. The only thing we have is pale vegetables. Recovered but with no one in the least concerned about what happened in the first place, he's forced to continue living with the monster who tried to kill him in the most cruel way. <br><br>Bunnicula subverts our expectations: we expect to discover that he is indeed a vampire, but in the end that's not the story at all. As in great Gothic novels like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1068109057" title="My review" rel="nofollow noopener">Uncle Silas</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/177295526" title="My review" rel="nofollow noopener">Lady Audley's Secret,</a> the real villain was inside the house: it's Chester, the psychopathic cat. Jealous of the attention paid to a new pet, he frames him as a monster and is barely stopped from murdering him. He's abetted by the dog, who hides a slavish complicity under his goofy doggishness. Horrifyingly, there are sequels to Bunnicula. Who knows what tortures they'll bring to this poor, defenseless bunny?</span>
  <a data-text-id="11783077271764995539" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_272592441" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/272592441" />
    <a title="Melissa Storm" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4257833-melissa-storm"><img alt="Melissa Storm" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1460032710p2/4257833.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/272592441?book_show_action=true">Feb 05, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa Storm" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa Storm" href="/user/show/4257833-melissa-storm">Melissa Storm</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4257833-melissa-storm?shelf=phoenix-s-bookshelf">phoenix-s-bookshelf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer272592441" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9823257202754280382">It’s only month #2 of <a href='http://www.emlynchand.com/2012/01/sign-up-for-the-2012-books-that-made-me-love-reading-challenge/' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>the “books that made me love reading" challenge</a>, and already, I’m noticing a pattern. Last month, <a href='http://www.emlynchand.com/2012/02/harold-and-the-purple-crayon-a-re-review-of-the-book-that-made-me-love-reading-in-the-first-place/' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>I re-reviewed Harold and the Purple Crayon</a>, a book that has had a profound influence on my life. I freely attribute my creativity to the inspiration I received from this happy little picture book, and now I realize that this month’s book, Bunnicula, has had an equally large impact on my life and personality.<br/><br/>Bunnicula made me smart. Seriously, it did.<br/><br/>Yes, I’m raising serious nat</span>
  <span id="freeText9823257202754280382" style="display:none">It’s only month #2 of <a href="http://www.emlynchand.com/2012/01/sign-up-for-the-2012-books-that-made-me-love-reading-challenge/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">the “books that made me love reading" challenge</a>, and already, I’m noticing a pattern. Last month, <a href="http://www.emlynchand.com/2012/02/harold-and-the-purple-crayon-a-re-review-of-the-book-that-made-me-love-reading-in-the-first-place/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">I re-reviewed Harold and the Purple Crayon</a>, a book that has had a profound influence on my life. I freely attribute my creativity to the inspiration I received from this happy little picture book, and now I realize that this month’s book, Bunnicula, has had an equally large impact on my life and personality.<br /><br />Bunnicula made me smart. Seriously, it did.<br /><br />Yes, I’m raising serious nature vs. nurture questions here, but the authors Howe &amp; Howe really deserve some credit. They didn’t dumb down their vocabulary to appeal to children, no. They let the big words and the references to classic literary works fly. The authors didn’t say, “Hey, wait a sec here. How are kids supposed to know about Dracula, or Treasure Island, or A Tale of Two Cities?” They said, “Hey, kids probably won’t know about these great books, but maybe after reading Bunnicula, they’ll search them out.”<br /><br />I really respect that about Bunnicula, and frankly, I don’t even remember the huge words being a problem when I was reading it as a kid. Maybe these things are less of an issue than adults think they are, just saying.<br /><br />Okay, so the title of the book clearly refers to our friend, Bunnicula, the vampire bunny wabbit. And the narrator is Harold, a mutt who loves to feast on chocolate cupcakes but never succumbs to their poison. Interesting...<br /><br />Now, <em>who</em>, you ask, <em>who is the star of this tome?</em> Why, Chester, the hair-brained, intellectual pussy cat, of course!<br /><br />I think I probably wanted to marry Chester when I was a little girl. That’s okay to admit, because children often want to marry parents or cartoon characters. Chester is a perfectly acceptable crush, thank you. (I also crushed major on Disney’s Aladdin, but that’s a story for another day.)<br /><br />The reasons why Chester is super dreamy abound. He’s intelligent, well-read, persistent, intuitive, funny, and cuddly. If you didn’t know I was talking about a fictional cat just now, you would probably be like, “Oh, sign me up for some of that!” Don’t lie to yourself, admit it!<br /><br />Sure, Chester isn’t always right about everything. Who is? But it’s fun to watch his misadventures unfold. Flights of fancy are fun, especially when you’re tucked comfortably into your Teenage Mutant Ninja Turtles sleeping bag with a flash light. Are you understanding who I was as a child now?<br /><br />Bunnicula was a great read for boys and girls alike. I should know, because I detested girly gook. I collected bugs and refused to play with dolls. Bunnicula wasn’t a story about a pampered princess; it was a nitty gritty tale of vegetables in peril. I liked that.<br /><br />Bunnicula was cute while still being terrifyingly ferocious. I’m sorry, Edward Cullen, but I’d take Bunnicula over you ANY DAY!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9823257202754280382" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3261690035" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3261690035" />
    <a title="YouKneeK" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25923230-youkneek"><img alt="YouKneeK" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1386369592p2/25923230.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3261690035?book_show_action=true">Apr 04, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="YouKneeK" class="user" itemprop="url" name="YouKneeK" href="/user/show/25923230-youkneek">YouKneeK</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/13348827-bunnicula">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25923230-youkneek?shelf=standalone">standalone</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25923230-youkneek?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25923230-youkneek?shelf=children">children</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3261690035" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14041573782362261860"><i>Bunnicula</i> is a cute little children’s book that I may or may not have read as a child. I was vaguely familiar with the story, but I don’t specifically remember reading it. Even as an adult it was pretty entertaining; it made a great change of pace and a fun diversion.<br/><br/>The story is set in the household of a family with a mother, a father, two bratty sons, a dog, and a cat. It’s told from the perspective of the dog. One night the human part of the family comes home with a bunny, but this bunny seem</span>
  <span id="freeText14041573782362261860" style="display:none"><i>Bunnicula</i> is a cute little children’s book that I may or may not have read as a child. I was vaguely familiar with the story, but I don’t specifically remember reading it. Even as an adult it was pretty entertaining; it made a great change of pace and a fun diversion.<br /><br />The story is set in the household of a family with a mother, a father, two bratty sons, a dog, and a cat. It’s told from the perspective of the dog. One night the human part of the family comes home with a bunny, but this bunny seems to have some alarming traits…<br /><br />It was a funny story and made me chuckle several times. I particularly liked Chester the cat whose cleverness and strangeness only slightly surpasses that of my own cat. I was a little disturbed to see how much chocolate the poor dog was fed, and I can’t help worrying a bit that children reading the book today might be inspired to feed their own dog chocolate after reading how happy it made Harold. Parental guidance suggested. ;)<br /><br />The edition I read had some brief and interesting details about how the book came about. It also had some artwork from various cover editions over the years, including the book covers published for other languages.</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14747695144631002125">I had completely forgotten about reading this book as a child until a conversation with my best friend likening someone to a bunny with red eyes and fangs. Whereupon she said, wait, I'm pretty sure that's actually a book isn't it? She looked it up and yes, yes it was. <br/><br/>BUNNICULA is one of those children's books that I love! Literary references and large vocabulary words interwoven into an adorable little story. Although I had forgotten about this book, not hard to do when you book carnivore like </span>
  <span id="freeText14747695144631002125" style="display:none">I had completely forgotten about reading this book as a child until a conversation with my best friend likening someone to a bunny with red eyes and fangs. Whereupon she said, wait, I'm pretty sure that's actually a book isn't it? She looked it up and yes, yes it was. <br /><br />BUNNICULA is one of those children's books that I love! Literary references and large vocabulary words interwoven into an adorable little story. Although I had forgotten about this book, not hard to do when you book carnivore like I do, I now remember really enjoying it as a child. <br /><br />It's written from Howard the dog's point of view which I always think is just so much fun. Full of lovely little references to Edgar Allan Poe and Robert Louis Stevenson, amongst others. Bunnicula is a bunny vampire who drains vegetables of their juices, could there be a better kids will be kids novel. Imagination is so important with children and this book just embodies that to me. It's not a life lessons book by any means, it's just for fun which I think is really great. </span>

<div id="review_1463367751" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1463367751" />
    <a title="Briar&#39;s Reviews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32054036-briar-s-reviews"><img alt="Briar&#39;s Reviews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1402183274p2/32054036.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1463367751?book_show_action=true">Mar 01, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Briar&#39;s Reviews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Briar&#39;s Reviews" href="/user/show/32054036-briar-s-reviews">Briar&#39;s Reviews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32054036-briar-s-reviews?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32054036-briar-s-reviews?shelf=cute">cute</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32054036-briar-s-reviews?shelf=crime-mystery-suspense">crime-mystery-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32054036-briar-s-reviews?shelf=drama">drama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32054036-briar-s-reviews?shelf=fun">fun</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32054036-briar-s-reviews?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32054036-briar-s-reviews?shelf=guilty-pleasure">guilty-pleasure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32054036-briar-s-reviews?shelf=top-books">top-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32054036-briar-s-reviews?shelf=family">family</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32054036-briar-s-reviews?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1463367751" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12197467705020285911">Back in the day, Bunnicula was THE book to read in elementary school. The class clambered to the front of the classroom to sit in our little circle and have story time. This book turned us all into little book loving zombies and we were desperate for more. Unfortunately, our school and teachers were only ever able to get the first book, but that didn't deter us. We all had it memorized by the end of the day.<br/><br/>Fast forward to 2020. I see this book in a local used bookstore and I decide, "Hey, why n</span>
  <span id="freeText12197467705020285911" style="display:none">Back in the day, Bunnicula was THE book to read in elementary school. The class clambered to the front of the classroom to sit in our little circle and have story time. This book turned us all into little book loving zombies and we were desperate for more. Unfortunately, our school and teachers were only ever able to get the first book, but that didn't deter us. We all had it memorized by the end of the day.<br /><br />Fast forward to 2020. I see this book in a local used bookstore and I decide, "Hey, why not read it again and see if it holds up?" I can see this book for what it is - an absolute delightful middle grade novel that introduces fun horror to youthful eyes. As an adult, it didn't hold up for me but I still have a special place in my heart for it. Who doesn't love Bunnicula? Seriously.<br /><br />Vampire Bunnies. It's such a unique idea and I LOVE it. This book sits with Goosebumps on my happy, little, Halloween-loving shelf. This bunny goes and drains vegetables, because obviously it was owned by Dracula! It's a fun concept and super silly! It's definitely a book I would recommend for parents and educators. Get your little readers into a spooky, Halloween spirit with this little gem!<br /><br />As an adult, it feels like a funny SNL skit. It's not scary to us because we know it's fiction but to little kids it's a potential nightmare (in a good way, it's not THAT scary). The anticipation as a child was not there as an adult, but I can still appreciate how wonderfully written this book is. It's short and sweet but packed full of story! <br /><br />Also, surprise ending! I forgot how this book ended so I was pleasantly surprised!<br /><br />The only negative I had with this book was some of the adult references: classic books, taxes, etc. Kids might not understand these terms, but if they have a great adult reader helping them along, it might be a good educational opportunity, I guess.<br /><br />Overall, this book is a childhood fave of mine that I would still highly recommend! It's so nostalgic for me and I truly miss the whimsical nature of reading these books!<br /><br />Four out of five stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12197467705020285911" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2895672046?book_show_action=true">Oct 13, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cori" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cori" href="/user/show/20906001-cori">Cori</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2895672046" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer9391587029094607487">All these people talking about the nostalgia behind reading these books as kids. And here I am, TODAY YEARS OLD, when I'm giggling like a kid reading about Chester, the crazy cat; Harold, the sweet dog; and...Bunnicula- dun, dun, DUUUUN. <br/><br/>But seriously, I loved the adorable innocence and hysterical capers of these animals.<br/><br/>The books are narrated by Harold, who is an unreliable narrator, constantly distracted by chocolate cupcakes and steak. He is buddies with Chester, the intelligent reading cat w</span>
  <span id="freeText9391587029094607487" style="display:none">All these people talking about the nostalgia behind reading these books as kids. And here I am, TODAY YEARS OLD, when I'm giggling like a kid reading about Chester, the crazy cat; Harold, the sweet dog; and...Bunnicula- dun, dun, DUUUUN. <br /><br />But seriously, I loved the adorable innocence and hysterical capers of these animals.<br /><br />The books are narrated by Harold, who is an unreliable narrator, constantly distracted by chocolate cupcakes and steak. He is buddies with Chester, the intelligent reading cat who may have some...issues, including narcissistic levels of pretention. And then there's Bunnicula. The vampire bunny who needs vegetable juice to survive. The family is so confused when they find white vegetables littering their kitchen floor, sucked clean of their juices. Oh, the carnage!<br /><br />And side-note: this book really seems to be more about Chester, the crazy cat, than Bunnicula. <br /><br />If you have kiddos, or are yourself a kiddo at heart (please say yes!), read this book! It's so much fun. <br /><br />I'd rate this book a G.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9391587029094607487" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_252434036" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/252434036" />
    <a title="Sara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1256603-sara"><img alt="Sara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596206765p2/1256603.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/252434036?book_show_action=true">Dec 28, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sara" href="/user/show/1256603-sara">Sara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1256603-sara?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1256603-sara?shelf=young-adult-supernatural-thriller-r">young-adult-supernatural-thriller-r</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer252434036" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4196647989287706321">One of my favorite memories of childhood was going to the library and getting the record of "Bunnicula" out to listen to. Lou Jacobi narrated it. There's a newer version now with Victor Garber but its Lou's nasally, sarcastic Chester the cat and sardonic, gentle Harold the dog that stays with me.<br/><br/>I love this book. Its one of those childhood experiences that I just treasure. The thing I recall most is this feeling of perfect contentment while it played. Even though the story, about a possibly vamp</span>
  <span id="freeText4196647989287706321" style="display:none">One of my favorite memories of childhood was going to the library and getting the record of "Bunnicula" out to listen to. Lou Jacobi narrated it. There's a newer version now with Victor Garber but its Lou's nasally, sarcastic Chester the cat and sardonic, gentle Harold the dog that stays with me.<br /><br />I love this book. Its one of those childhood experiences that I just treasure. The thing I recall most is this feeling of perfect contentment while it played. Even though the story, about a possibly vampiric bunny rabbit invading the home of a cat with literary aspirations and a well meaning, bumbling sheep dog, was supposed to give me the willies it always just made me happy.<br /><br />I must have listened to this a hundred times. I loved it so much that when its sequels <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/183436.The_Celery_Stalks_at_Midnight__Bunnicula___3_" title="The Celery Stalks at Midnight (Bunnicula, #3) by James Howe" rel="nofollow noopener">The Celery Stalks at Midnight</a> and my especial favorite <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/443658.Howliday_Inn__Bunnicula___2_" title="Howliday Inn (Bunnicula, #2) by James Howe" rel="nofollow noopener">Howliday Inn</a> came out I actually recorded my own versions on my dad's tape deck. I'd sit for literally hours on the floor by our old out of tune piano doing all the voices and playing it back to make sure it was perfect. <br /><br />Harold, the lovable dog, is the narrator. While his companion Chester (named for G.K. Chesterton) likes to think he's a blundering moron, its Harold's lovable, affable nature that inevitably gets them out of the sticky situations Chester gets them into. When their family, the Monroe's, come home from a rainy night at the movies with a small shoebox containing a tiny, baby bunny it takes Chester no time at all to become convinced that Bunnicula (so named because the Monroe's were seeing "Dracula" and because the markings on his fur make it look like he's wearing a black cape) is an ACTUAL vampire. And admittedly the evidence is pretty staggering. Bunnicula keeps escaping his cage without opening the door and random vegetables keep turning up drained of all their juice. Clearly something very strange is going on. <br /><br />The mystery is just so charming and unique and the message, different doesn't have to equal bad, is understated enough to avoid being preachy. James Howe absolutely never panders to his audience, something even at the ripe old age of 10 or 11 I recognized and abhorred in most books for kids my age. He clearly recognized that kids want to hear stories! Sure you can offer little insights about tolerance and acceptance but it doesn't need to be the bloody Bernstein Bears all the damn time. <br /><br />This book and its sequels are funny but they're also genuine. Its a little thing to grab on to but one of my favorite parts of these books is how the hijinks that always ensue are inevitably because Harold and Chester are pets and therefore not privy to the "reality" of whats happening in the house. Everything is through the lens of them being, well, animals! Its subtle but its soooo perfect. Not only does it lay the groundwork for all the slapstick comedy it makes younger readers feel super smart when they figure things out before our hero's do!<br /><br />Something equally small that should be annoying but somehow adds to the charm is that its pretty obvious Mr. Jacobi didn't read his source material ahead of time or at least more than once. There's times when his sentences run on or a character voice is used for the wrong animal. I can very clearly hear my personal favorite moment even as I type this. Pete, the hormonal, teenage Monroe son is sarcastically saying goodnight to the animals and Harold isn't having it.<br /><br />"Goodnight, smelly Harold. Goodnight, dumb Chester." I drooled on Pete's foot.<br /><br />But the way Jacobi reads it it comes out like this;<br /><br />"Goodnight smelly Harold Goodnight dumb Chester I drooled on Pete's foot."<br /><br />I have no idea why, but I just love that. <br /><br />I deeply regret losing my silly little recordings a very long time ago but I will never, ever forget those afternoons I spent sitting cross legged on the floor reading away like a little VO star or lying on the couch letting Mr. Jacobi lull me into the blissful trance that only a truly wonderful story can provide.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4196647989287706321" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_317105288" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/317105288" />
    <a title="Michelle Isenhoff" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5319195-michelle-isenhoff"><img alt="Michelle Isenhoff" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1556827290p2/5319195.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/317105288?book_show_action=true">Apr 22, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michelle Isenhoff" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michelle Isenhoff" href="/user/show/5319195-michelle-isenhoff">Michelle Isenhoff</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer317105288" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14855754717913518815">I first met Chester and Harold as a kid and fell in love with them. If you haven’t encountered these two yet, let me introduce you. Chester is a highly educated cat with a vivid imagination. One of his delights is to listen to his owner, a college English professor, practice class lectures. He’s widely read, and especially favors Edgar Allen Poe. Harold isn’t quite as intellectual as Chester, but he does have a good deal more common sense. He’s also the one who wrote and delivered the first manu</span>
  <span id="freeText14855754717913518815" style="display:none">I first met Chester and Harold as a kid and fell in love with them. If you haven’t encountered these two yet, let me introduce you. Chester is a highly educated cat with a vivid imagination. One of his delights is to listen to his owner, a college English professor, practice class lectures. He’s widely read, and especially favors Edgar Allen Poe. Harold isn’t quite as intellectual as Chester, but he does have a good deal more common sense. He’s also the one who wrote and delivered the first manuscript of this story. Mr. Howe confesses to being only the publisher.<br /><br />In this first installment of Chester and Harold’s adventures, a baby bunny comes to live with the Monroe family. But he’s found at a Dracula movie, he has strange markings and oddly pointed teeth, and the note found in his basket is an obscure dialect of the Carpathian mountain region (fortunately, Harold is familiar with the language due to his varied ancestry), which is to say, Transylvania. When a variety of vegetables show up with tiny teeth marks and all juice and color drained from them, Chester puts two and two together and turns to his copy of The Mark of the Vampire. The lengths he goes to to protect his family from this imagined threat nearly get him tossed out of the house and left my boys and I howling with laughter!<br /><br />Bunnicula is a short read, coming in at only 98 pages, but they’re full of fun and wit. I’d estimate a third-grade independent reading level and an easy first grade listening level. The cadence, the dialogue, and the outrageous antics of our two heroes make this a superb read aloud. No matter your age, I highly encourage you to pick this one up!!<br /><br />James Howe has written several related stories. They haven’t received the same acclaim as Bunnicula, but I own Howliday Inn, and I love it almost as much. (Watch for my review soon.) I have not read the others.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14855754717913518815" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2572773586" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2572773586" />
    <a title="Matt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16796020-matt"><img alt="Matt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1452866952p2/16796020.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2572773586?book_show_action=true">Oct 24, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matt" href="/user/show/16796020-matt">Matt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover " href="/book/show/34683447-bunnicula">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2572773586" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2345552170397909422">A definite blast from the past. This was very popular when I was growing up and I haven’t read it in over 20 years so I figured the Halloween season this year would be perfect to revisit this children’s horror classic. This was a lot of fun. I loved our narrator Harold, the dog, and his friends Chester, and Bunnicula. There is a nice infusion of humor, in addition to the light hearted horror, into the story and I think it would be enjoyed by readers of all ages. A wonderful read. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_137107484" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/137107484" />
    <a title="Drebbles" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1862888-drebbles"><img alt="Drebbles" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1365895783p2/1862888.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/137107484?book_show_action=true">Dec 29, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Drebbles" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Drebbles" href="/user/show/1862888-drebbles">Drebbles</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1862888-drebbles?shelf=2010">2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer137107484" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4178226406948973213">Howard the Dog and Chester the Cat enjoy living with their humans - Harold especially likes Toby who enjoys feasts that he shares with Harold. So when the family brings home a bunny they name Bunnicula, it isn't surprising that Harold and Chester are a bit jealous of the attention the family focuses on Bunnicula. But Chester's jealousy soon turns into the suspicion that Bunnicula is a vampire. He sets out to prove it - no matter what the cost. <br/><br/>Although "Bunnicula" is aimed at readers ages 8 - 12</span>
  <span id="freeText4178226406948973213" style="display:none">Howard the Dog and Chester the Cat enjoy living with their humans - Harold especially likes Toby who enjoys feasts that he shares with Harold. So when the family brings home a bunny they name Bunnicula, it isn't surprising that Harold and Chester are a bit jealous of the attention the family focuses on Bunnicula. But Chester's jealousy soon turns into the suspicion that Bunnicula is a vampire. He sets out to prove it - no matter what the cost. <br /><br />Although "Bunnicula" is aimed at readers ages 8 - 12, it is a delightful book for readers of all ages. It is written in the first person from Harold's point of view and it is a lot of fun reading what Harold thinks about the goings on as well as his constant focus on food. Also fun to read is Chester's ongoing battle to prove Bunnicula is a vampire and how his efforts baffle the family who think Chester is just being a cat. Harold and Chester remind me a lot of the Satchel and Bucky characters in the Get Fuzzy comic strip although Chester is not nearly as mean as Bucky. There is a wonderful sense of humor throughout the book and the vampire elements are never scary and played for fun. In fact, I laughed out loud at times especially when Chester tries to steak..er stake Bunnicula. <br /><br />"Bunnicula" (the first of many books in the Bunnicula series) is a delightfully funny book for readers young and old. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4178226406948973213" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2139322281" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2139322281" />
    <a title="Tito the Incognito" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/72007667-tito-the-incognito"><img alt="Tito the Incognito" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1506727946p2/72007667.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2139322281?book_show_action=true">Sep 30, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tito the Incognito" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tito the Incognito" href="/user/show/72007667-tito-the-incognito">Tito the Incognito</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780380510948" href="/book/show/563901.Bunnicula">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">4th &amp; 5th graders </span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/72007667-tito-the-incognito?shelf=assigned-in-school">assigned-in-school</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/72007667-tito-the-incognito?shelf=childrens-books">childrens-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2139322281" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14484313072290914210">Way back when I was in the fourth grade (I'm in my 30s now, so obviously quite some time ago) my teacher read this book aloud to the class and I enjoyed it so much that I bugged my parents to buy it for me. I'd highly recommend Bunnicula, as well as its sequels, to anyone seeking reading material for their nine or ten-year-old children as it's a delightful read. It's humorous, the characters are endearing, and the plot will keep your kids interested enough that they'll want to keep reading until</span>
  <span id="freeText14484313072290914210" style="display:none">Way back when I was in the fourth grade (I'm in my 30s now, so obviously quite some time ago) my teacher read this book aloud to the class and I enjoyed it so much that I bugged my parents to buy it for me. I'd highly recommend Bunnicula, as well as its sequels, to anyone seeking reading material for their nine or ten-year-old children as it's a delightful read. It's humorous, the characters are endearing, and the plot will keep your kids interested enough that they'll want to keep reading until the end. Or at least that was the case for me; I could not put down any of the books in the Bunnicula series once I started reading them. This book is undoubtedly a page turner, at least for the elementary school aged crowd anyway. But if you read it with (or aloud to) your child, I'm willing to bet that you'll find yourself enjoying it too. Bunnicula truly stands out as one of the most memorable books of my childhood, one that I'll always reflect back upon with fondness.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_158117075" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/158117075" />
    <a title="Corinne Edwards" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/875001-corinne-edwards"><img alt="Corinne Edwards" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1569257331p2/875001.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/158117075?book_show_action=true">Apr 01, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Corinne Edwards" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Corinne Edwards" href="/user/show/875001-corinne-edwards">Corinne Edwards</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/875001-corinne-edwards?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/875001-corinne-edwards?shelf=childrens-literature">childrens-literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/875001-corinne-edwards?shelf=anthropormorphism">anthropormorphism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/875001-corinne-edwards?shelf=xavier">xavier</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/875001-corinne-edwards?shelf=preston">preston</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/875001-corinne-edwards?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/875001-corinne-edwards?shelf=laugh-out-loud">laugh-out-loud</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/875001-corinne-edwards?shelf=dogs">dogs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/875001-corinne-edwards?shelf=cats">cats</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/875001-corinne-edwards?shelf=rabbits">rabbits</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer158117075" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2344277262599929665">I remember hearing about this little "vampire" bunny when I was a kid, but the story never interested me. Shame on me, because I read it outloud to my two little boys this past week and had a ball. Our narrator is the loyal, if not slightly blustering, dog Harold. When their family discovers a WHITE tomato, Harold's scheming cat-friend Chester is convinced that the family's new bunny is the culprit. A juice sucking BUNNY? That is just funny, in fact, my boys were in hysterics more than once, tha</span>
  <span id="freeText2344277262599929665" style="display:none">I remember hearing about this little "vampire" bunny when I was a kid, but the story never interested me. Shame on me, because I read it outloud to my two little boys this past week and had a ball. Our narrator is the loyal, if not slightly blustering, dog Harold. When their family discovers a WHITE tomato, Harold's scheming cat-friend Chester is convinced that the family's new bunny is the culprit. A juice sucking BUNNY? That is just funny, in fact, my boys were in hysterics more than once, thanks to Chester's hair-brained plans to rescue the family from their fang-toothed pet.<br /><br />I can see why this one is a classic, my boys were always begging for more. I think we'll search out more books in this charming and clever series. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2344277262599929665" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

Good lesson to take in I think. 4, anemic vegetable, stars!</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('SuKaWcLVwyPjIUCnh+XPNtM/yBlZveEk9BQJTraXtwfuUT/KzSoG+/0bafpWXF4NEhj3eIWSAut9/il94ZrQqg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('EYAGGg1CorltH/KhwEaUdpe42DV4CkDVNfkdgfw0ef21M6OJAr1nYXMl2/wR/wVNVp/nVKQloxq8Ez2yqzkeUA==')})
  }

What ensues is an altogether captivating spin on the city mouse/country mouse story, as Chester adjusts to the bustle of the big city. Despite the cricket\'s comfortable matchbox bed (with Kleenex sheets); the fancy, seven-tiered pagoda cricket cage from Sai Fong\'s novelty shop; tasty mulberry leaves; the jolly company of Tucker Mouse and Harry Cat; and even his new-found fame as &quot;the most famous musician in New York City,&quot; Chester begins to miss his peaceful life in the Connecticut countryside. The Cricket in Times Square--a Newbery Honor Book in 1961--is charmingly illustrated by the well-loved Garth Williams, and the tiniest details of this elegantly spun, vividly told, surprisingly suspenseful tale will stick with children for years and years.
